## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. The inclusion of explicit time dependence suggests possible non-autonomous effects such as seasonal variation, time-varying carrying capacity, or environmental forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/population modeling)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect, negative growth at low density)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (proportional harvesting term)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield harvesting)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Seasonal logistic: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * P * (1 - c3 * P) (periodic environmental forcing on logistic growth)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with hyperbolic saturation)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth model)
- Time-decaying growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * t) (growth rate diminishing with time due to resource depletion)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (cubic density dependence)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent feedback → multiplicative factor (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)**n) representing carrying capacity limitation
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → additional multiplicative factor (P*c - 1) creating a lower critical threshold
- Explicit time dependence in growth rate → coefficient modulated by t, e.g., c0*(1 + f(t)), suggesting environmental change or seasonality
- Gompertz-type asymmetry → log(c/P) factor indicating growth rate proportional to logarithmic distance from carrying capacity
- Harvesting or mortality sink → additive negative term independent of or weakly dependent on P, representing external removal
- Ratio-dependent regulation → P/(1 + c*P) or P/(1 + c*P**2) representing interference or handling time in resource competition
- Population-intrinsic nonlinearity → P**c with fractional exponent c representing metabolic scaling or surface-volume relationships
- Delayed environmental degradation → growth rate multiplied by decreasing function of t such as exp(-c*t) or 1/(1+c*t)

**GT:** `0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

Let me simplify the GT:
- First term: `0.1728*P - 0.003559*P²` (a linear + quadratic in P)
- Second term: `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))` (a sigmoid-weighted term)

The GT has the form: **c0*P + c1*P² + c2*P/(1 + exp(c3 + c4*P))**

Key observations about the GT:
1. It depends only on P, NOT on t
2. It contains a **sigmoid function** (logistic function involving exp)
3. The basis functions are: P, P², and P/(1+exp(linear in P))

Now let me check each candidate. For a candidate to match, it must:
- Be able to eliminate all t-dependent terms (by setting their coefficients to 0)
- Contain basis functions that can reproduce the sigmoid term

**Critical filter:** The sigmoid term `P/(1 + exp(c*P + d))` cannot be represented by:
- Polynomials in P
- Power functions P^c
- Rational functions like 1/(P+c)^n
- Simple exponentials exp(c*P)

Let me check which candidates have terms that could potentially match the sigmoid:

Most candidates contain terms like:
- `P**c2*c3` (power law - cannot match sigmoid)
- `1/(P+c)^n` (rational - cannot match sigmoid)
- `exp(P*c)` (exponential - not sigmoid)
- `t`-dependent terms (can be zeroed)
- `log(...)` terms

**None of these basis functions can reproduce a sigmoid function `P/(1+exp(c*P+d))`.**

The sigmoid function `1/(1+exp(-x))` is fundamentally different from:
- Any polynomial or rational function
- Any power function P^c
- Any simple exponential exp(cP)
- Any logarithm

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), no combination of polynomials, power laws, rational functions, exponentials, or logarithms of the forms present in the candidates can exactly equal a sigmoid function for all P.

Let me verify each candidate systematically - after zeroing t-dependent terms, what remains?

For all candidates, after setting t-coefficients to 0, the remaining terms are combinations of: P², P, P^c, 1/(P+c)^n, exp(cP), log(cP+1), constants, P^(-2), and similar. None of these can produce the sigmoid `P/(1+exp(linear in P))`.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
